Analysis of manufacturing AI transformation (AX) trends revealed that AI is emerging as a core competitive advantage in the manufacturing industry, going beyond simple process automation.

Among the key trends, predictive maintenance, smart logistics, and AI quality inspection have established themselves as core technologies maximizing productivity and efficiency. They predict equipment failures, optimize supply chains, and significantly reduce defect rates. Additionally, Digital Twin, which replicates the real world virtually for simulation, and Physical AI, which understands physical laws, are gaining attention as next-generation innovative technologies.

While the adoption of these technologies offers opportunities to innovate across the entire manufacturing value chain, it simultaneously presents challenges such as the AI literacy gap (AI understanding and utilization capabilities) and the difficulty of digital transformation for small and medium-sized enterprises. Therefore, for a successful AI transformation, an integrated approach that combines technology adoption with role-based talent development and data governance establishment is essential.

Smart logistics combines end-to-end visibility, AI-driven predictive intelligence, and full-stage automation to transform reactive operations into proactive and semi-autonomous operations. Prioritize areas with numerous micro-decisions, significant cost pressures, and limitations of manual planning, and aim for quick ROI in transportation (route/load optimization), demand & inventory, warehousing (slotting, RPA, labor), and exceptions & reverse logistics. Start small, secure the data foundation (MDM alignment, WMS/TMS/ERP/IoT integration, real-time telematics) and align operations, IT, and management, and manage the pilot â†’ measure â†’ scale process with KPIs such as OTIF, transportation cost/shipment, inventory turnover, lead time, picking productivity, forecast MAPE, and exception handling lead time.

By designing real-time visibility and a sense-analyze-act control loop based on the smart manufacturing stack (IoT + Edge + Digital Twin), and combining AI operational priorities (predictive maintenance for high-value and bottleneck equipment, vision quality, generative AI-based work standard/training material automation) with the phased ROI gate expansion of AMR, AGV, and cobots, OEE improvement and a reduction in run-up time can be quickly achieved. The 2025 manufacturing trends are organized around eight axes, presenting application examples and expected effects for each area. The core involves smart manufacturing based on IoT, edge, and digital twin; operationalization of AI such as predictive maintenance, vision inspection, and generative AI; phased ROI management for the introduction of AMR/cobots; workforce transformation through skill matrices and real-time training; and reducing supply chain risks through nearshoring, multisourcing, blockchain, and AI prediction. Additionally, it presents circular economy models and ESG data automation, ensuring scalability through integrated data platforms and OT cybersecurity, and a pilot roadmap for new technologies such as 5G, agentic AI, and quantum. Cases involving fresh food and global cosmetics suggest that real-time visibility and data governance have a practical effect on waste reduction, quality and regulatory compliance, and lead time reduction. Practically, it is useful for selecting priority use cases, establishing data pipelines and governance, and formulating a phased pilot-to-scale strategy.

A pipeline is proposed that performs outlier detection on surface changes in 3D point clouds based on the 90th percentile, followed by density-based clustering, and then classifies scratches, round, and elongated bumps using rule-based methods/ML. This approach demonstrates the feasibility of field application with quantitative results such as dimensional errors (H+2.56%, Wâˆ’3.28%). Establishing a closed loop by linking edge GPU inspection results with robot sorting and MES via OPC UA/MQTT, managing KPIs (precision, recall, cycle time, missed/false detections) and MSA (GRR, Cg/Cgk), and reducing false detections through CAD feature masking, multi-sensor fusion, dynamic thresholding, and self-correction is practically effective.

ë³¸ ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” 3D í¬ì¸íŠ¸ í´ë¼ìš°ë“œì—ì„œ êµ­ë¶€ í‘œë©´ ë³€ë™ì˜ ìƒìœ„ 10%ë¥¼ ê²°í•¨ í›„ë³´ë¡œ í‘œì‹œí•˜ê³ , ë°€ë„ ê¸°ë°˜ êµ°ì§‘í™”ë¡œ ê²°í•¨ì„ ë¬¶ì–´ ì‚¬ì „ ê¸°ì¤€ì— ë”°ë¼ ìœ í˜•ì„ ë¶„ë¥˜í•œ ë’¤, ê²°ê³¼ë¥¼ ë¡œë´‡ ì†ŒíŒ…ìœ¼ë¡œ ì—°ê³„í•œ ì¸ë¼ì¸ ê²€ì‚¬ íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸ì„ ì œì‹œí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê²°í•¨ ì¤‘ì‹¬ì¢Œí‘œ, ë¹„ìœ¨, ì¹˜ìˆ˜ ì˜¤ì°¨ ë“± ì •ëŸ‰ ì§€í‘œì™€ ì‹¤í—˜ ê²°ê³¼ í‘œê°€ ì œê³µë˜ì–´ ì‹¤ë¬´ ì ìš© ì‹œ ë ˆí¼ëŸ°ìŠ¤ë¡œ ìœ ìš©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. AX ê´€ì ì—ì„œëŠ” KPI/MSA ê´€ë¦¬ ì²´ê³„ í™•ë¦½, CAD í”¼ì²˜ ë§ˆìŠ¤í‚¹ê³¼ ë©€í‹°ì„¼ì„œ ìœµí•©ì„ í†µí•œ ì˜¤ê²€ ì €ê°, ì—£ì§€ ì—°ì‚° ë° OPC UA/MQTT ì—°ë™ìœ¼ë¡œ MESÂ·ë¡œë´‡ê¹Œì§€ í†µí•©í•˜ëŠ” í™•ì¥ì´ ê¶Œì¥ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. This study presents an inline inspection pipeline that identifies the top 10% of local surface variations in 3D point clouds as defect candidates, clusters defects using density-based clustering, then classifies their types according to predefined criteria, and links the results to robot sorting. Quantitative indicators such as defect centroid coordinates, ratio, and dimensional error, along with tables of experimental results, are provided, which are useful as references for practical application. From an AX perspective, an expansion is recommended that includes the establishment of KPI/MSA management systems, reduction of inspection errors through CAD feature masking and multi-sensor fusion, and integration up to MES and robots via edge computing and OPC UA/MQTT interoperation.

The bottleneck in AI adoption in the manufacturing industry is not technology but AI literacy; the fact that less than 10% of employees in 76% of manufacturers utilize AI indicates delays in pilot-to-on-site application scaling and the risk of ROI erosion. This paper clearly demonstrates that digital agility mediates the path through which 'Lean 4.0,' combining Lean Manufacturing with IIoT/AI/CPS/Analytics, leads to operational excellence in the Industry 4.0 transition of SMEs. For practical application, it recommends a roadmap that combines soft elements such as leadership, capability development, and empowerment with hard practices such as TPM, SPC, predictive maintenance, and real-time monitoring, and progresses through maturity diagnosis â†’ low-cost pilot (e.g., condition-based monitoring of critical equipment) â†’ on-site upskilling and standard work-data integration â†’ OPC UA/MQTT-based interoperability and data governance â†’ verification and expansion with KPIs such as OEE/Lead Time/FPY/MTBF. AI-embedded ERP transforms manufacturing operations from reactive to proactive, mitigating demand fluctuations, supply chain risks, and labor shortages, and increasing decision-making speed, cost efficiency, and operational resilience. As priority use cases, directly reduce process losses and lead times by selecting demand forecasting and supply chain optimization, predictive maintenance and intelligent scheduling, and repetitive task automation. For implementation, an effective approach involves data standardization/MDM, preparation of integrated architecture (API), combined data and domain capabilities, change management, and value-based governance, phasing from pilot to scale and managing performance with KPIs (prediction accuracy, downtime, schedule adherence, inventory turnover).

The article presents how AI transforms manufacturing ERP into a proactive decision-making platform and its priority application areas (demand/supply chain, predictive maintenance/quality, scheduling, automation). The government's 7-year roadmap for 'Physical AI' transition (robotics, automotive, shipbuilding, home appliances, drones, factories, semiconductors), along with its 100 trillion won growth fund and preliminary feasibility study exemption policy, will realign manufacturers' CAPEX and PoC priorities, presenting an opportunity to preempt pilot projects, testbeds, and standardization tasks through consortia of large corporations, mid-sized companies/startups, and academia. From a process perspective, it is advisable to prioritize promoting AI vision inspection, predictive maintenance, autonomous logistics, and on-device/edge-based product intelligence, and to set 2030 targets such as humanoid collaboration and fully autonomous ships as benchmarks for the mid-to-long-term roadmap. However, in preparation for strengthened industrial safety responsibilities and penalties, simultaneously implement EHS data digitization, integrated safety management for subcontractors, and digital work permits; and, centered around the PMO, execute continuous monitoring of government RFPs, internal technology roadmap mapping, and policy change scenario planning.

The government plans to present a 7-year transformation plan for 7 major manufacturing industries, including robotics, automobiles, shipbuilding, home appliances, drones, factories, and semiconductors, centering on 'Physical AI,' and aims to drive investment with a 100 trillion won fund and exemption from preliminary feasibility studies. Simultaneously, with the announced strengthening of prime contractors' responsibility for workers of partner companies and an increase in industrial safety penalties, regulatory compliance costs will rise. For manufacturers, it is practically effective to expedite responding to government projects based on consortia, aligning smart factory and product AI roadmaps, and the digital transformation of EHS and partner company safety, while simultaneously implementing scenario and cash flow management in preparation for uncertainties in funding and execution.

This project implements PINN-based physical AI as an integrated system for on-site data collection, modeling, and validation to enhance the precision of prediction and control for physics-governed processes such as cutting, forming, heat treatment, and injection molding, and accelerates commercialization through global collaboration. To maximize effectiveness, upon adoption, it is essential to clarify the hybrid operation of edge real-time inference and cloud learning, alongside standards for sensor time synchronization, tag schemas, and metadata, data governance, IP and data usage rights, and pilot-to-rollout plans based on KPIs (defect rate, cycle time, energy, OEE). For initial utilization, effective applications include the reduction of setup time through machining condition-quality surrogates, defect reduction through heat treatment/forming simulation calibration, and online quality prediction and closed-loop control.

Gyeongnam National University of Science and Technology will lead a 320 billion KRW PINN-based manufacturing integrated data collection and demonstration project. Aiming for ultra-precision control, it will develop and demonstrate physics-based AI models for each industry, and accelerate commercialization by sharing data and models with companies through an on-site data collection system and the GNAIX platform. It is effective for manufacturers to prepare an edge-cloud architecture, standardized tagging/metadata, data governance, and a KPI-centric pilot-to-scale-up roadmap. PINN is effective in areas such as process simulation calibration, condition optimization, and online quality prediction/closed-loop control, and a strategy of introducing physics AI agents combined with digital twins with phased HITL operation is recommended.

Since the government will support AI convergence in 7 major manufacturing sectors such as robotics, automotive, shipbuilding, home appliances, drones, smart factories, and semiconductors through financial, tax, and regulatory sandbox measures, manufacturers should align their AI roadmaps with the policy framework, clarify KPI/ROI hypotheses (such as OEE, defect rate, and energy consumption) for initiatives like predictive maintenance, AI vision inspection, process scheduling/AMR, energy optimization, and digital twin, pursuing them from PoC per line to cell expansion and then factory-wide deployment, and also prepare early for subsidy and tax benefit applications. Additionally, utilizing 'AI Hangeul' and talent development infrastructure, support on-site Q&A, safety training, and change management for SOPs, equipment manuals, and quality knowledge using Korean LLMs; proactively establish data lineage, model validation, OT security, and robot/drone safety certification; and mitigate risks of excess capacity through high-value-added, high-mix production, energy efficiency, and servitization (RaaS, predictive maintenance).

The core point is that the Korean government will intensively provide funding, tax benefits, and regulatory relief to 7 major manufacturing sectors through an AI-centric growth strategy. Manufacturers should select AI application tasks starting from areas with immediate high impact, such as predictive maintenance, vision inspection, scheduling, autonomous logistics, and energy optimization, and clearly define KPIs, data requirements, and ROI to actively utilize support programs and regulatory sandboxes. To achieve results from AI adoption, first begin with 'housekeeping' of manufacturing data: systematically inspect and improve common flaws such as missing data, duplication, timestamp/unit inconsistencies, versioning issues, and calibration errors, and establish data collection and retention priorities linked to KPIs like OEE, yield, lead time, and energy costs. Establish a data dictionary, standard schema, labeling rules, ETL automation, and governance/MDM, and through a phased roadmap of data diagnosis â†’ application of quality rules â†’ integration â†’ analysis/modeling, along with ROI tracking (defect rate, downtime, scrap, energy savings), expand pilot programs for predictive maintenance, process optimization, and anomaly detection. We propose a practical approach that supplements PoC costs and capability gaps by leveraging industry best practices and resources/funding from local universities.

This event focuses on establishing the data foundation (quality, standards, governance) that manufacturers must build before AI adoption. It covers 11 common data defects, how to link data types with strategic KPIs, and guides through the process of transforming raw data into actionable intelligence (data dictionaries, standards, ETL, quality rules). Through manufacturing company case studies, one can learn about defining pilot scope, phased rollout, and methods for tracking ROI, and strategies for receiving support for PoC and capability development through university resources and funding are also presented. It is useful for safely expanding use cases such as predictive maintenance and process optimization, through practical, hands-on data structuring and prioritization without overstatement.

Through Agentic AI (Executive Copilot), dynamic work instruction/SOP generation, quality anomaly detection leading to immediate CAPA, predictive and prescriptive maintenance, and constraint-based scheduling can be automated in a closed-loop, simultaneously improving OEE, FPY, delivery time, and energy metrics. Actual cases such as Hadrian, Elementary, and MaintainX prove the implementation path. For success, an integrated data layer, OT-IT connectivity, a reliable RAG knowledge base, an edge-cloud hybrid architecture, role-based governance, and human-in-the-loop and digital twin-based testing are required. The recommended roadmap is: after selecting KPI-based use cases, PoC leading to cell/line expansion, legacy integration with standard APIs and orchestration, on-site copilot training and change management, and continuous improvement with a performance dashboard (including cyber and environmental cost management).

This article proposes a strategy to automate and augment work instructions, scheduling, quality, maintenance, and logistics in a closed loop through agentic AI (super-agents) deployed in factory floors. For success, digital thread-based data consistency, OT-IT integration, governance including RAG (Retrieval-Augmented Generation) and access control, and safety verification through a digital twin sandbox are essential. Implementation is carried out by selecting KPI-centric use cases, establishing a pilot-to-scale roadmap, utilizing standard APIs and orchestration, and providing copilot training tailored to each on-site job function. Through simultaneous optimization, including energy and carbon metrics, sustainability and ROI can be achieved together.

í†µí•© ì¸ì‚¬ì´íŠ¸:Consolidated Insight:
ë¬¼ë¦¬Â·í™”í•™ ê¸°ë°˜ ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆì„ AIì™€ ê²°í•©í•´ ì „ê·¹ ë‘ê»˜, ì…ì ë°˜ê²½, í™•ì‚°ê³„ìˆ˜ ë“± ì„¤ê³„ íŒŒë¼ë¯¸í„° ìˆ˜ì¤€ì—ì„œ ì—´í™” ì›ì¸ì„ ë¶„ë¦¬Â·ì„¤ëª…í•˜ë©°, SOH/ìˆ˜ëª… ì˜ˆì¸¡ ì •í™•ë„ë¥¼ ìµœëŒ€ 65~69% ë†’ì—¬ í’ˆì§ˆê´€ë¦¬ì™€ ROIë¥¼ ë™ì‹œì— ì…ì¦í•œë‹¤. ì•½ 1ì´ˆ ì´ë‚´ ì—£ì§€ ì¶”ë¡ ê³¼ ì§§ì€ ì¶©ì „ êµ¬ê°„ ë°ì´í„°ë§Œìœ¼ë¡œ í˜•ì„±Â·íŒ¨í‚¤ì§•Â·EOL ê³µì •ì—ì„œ ë¹ ë¥¸ ìŠ¤í¬ë¦¬ë‹, ì´ìƒ ì¡°ê¸°ê²€ì¶œ, ì¬ì‘ì—… ìë™í™”ê°€ ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ë©°, ì…€ë³„ íŠ¹ì„±ì— ë§ì¶˜ ì¶©ì „/ë°¸ëŸ°ì‹± ë ˆì‹œí”¼ ìµœì í™”ê¹Œì§€ ì§€ì›í•œë‹¤. ë„ì… ì‹œ í™”í•™ê³„ë³„ ê²€ì¦Â·íŒŒë¼ë¯¸í„° ì´ˆê¸°í™”Â·ì˜¨ë„/ì „ë¥˜ ë³´ì • ë“± ìº˜ë¦¬ë¸Œë ˆì´ì…˜ê³¼ MES/PLMÂ·BMS ì—°ë™ì„ í†µí•´ ì„¤ê³„â€“ê³µì •â€“ìš´í–‰ ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ ì‡ëŠ” ë””ì§€í„¸ ìŠ¤ë ˆë“œë¥¼ ê°•í™”í•˜ë©´ íš¨ê³¼ë¥¼ ê·¹ëŒ€í™”í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤. By combining physics and chemistry-based digital twins with AI, it separates and explains degradation causes at the level of design parameters such as electrode thickness, particle radius, and diffusion coefficient, and simultaneously demonstrates quality management and ROI by increasing SOH/lifetime prediction accuracy by up to 65-69%. With edge inference within approximately 1 second and using only data from short charging segments, it enables rapid screening, early anomaly detection, and rework automation in the formation, packaging, and EOL processes, and even supports the optimization of charging/balancing recipes tailored to individual cell characteristics. Upon implementation, the effects can be maximized by strengthening the digital thread that connects design-process-operation data, through calibration (such as chemical system-specific verification, parameter initialization, and temperature/current compensation) and integration with MES/PLM and BMS.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ìŠ¤ì›¨ë´ ì—°êµ¬ì§„ì˜ ë¬¼ë¦¬ê¸°ë°˜ AI ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ ëª¨ë¸ì€ ì„¤ê³„ íŒŒë¼ë¯¸í„°ë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•´ ë°°í„°ë¦¬ ì—´í™”ë¥¼ ì •ë°€ ì¶”ì í•˜ë©°, ì§§ì€ ì¶©ì „ ë°ì´í„°ë¡œ 1ì´ˆ ë‚´ SOH/ìˆ˜ëª… ì˜ˆì¸¡ì„ ì œê³µí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê¸°ì¡´ ëŒ€ë¹„ ìµœëŒ€ 65%/69% ì„±ëŠ¥ ê°œì„ ì€ í˜•ì„±ê³µì •Â·EOL ê²€ì‚¬ì—ì„œ ë¹ ë¥¸ ì„ ë³„ê³¼ ì´ìƒ ì¡°ê¸°ê²€ì¶œ, BMSì˜ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ìƒíƒœê´€ë¦¬ ë° ì¶©Â·ë°©ì „ ë ˆì‹œí”¼ ìµœì í™”ì— ìœ ìš©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ” ì„¤ê³„-ê³µì •-ìš´í–‰ ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ ì‡ëŠ” ë””ì§€í„¸ ìŠ¤ë ˆë“œë¥¼ ê°•í™”í•˜ê³ , ë³´ì¦ë¹„ì™€ ì•ˆì „ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ë‚®ì¶œ ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ì „ëµì  ë„ì… ê°€ì¹˜ê°€ í½ë‹ˆë‹¤. í™”í•™ê³„ ë‹¤ë³€í™” ê²€ì¦, íŒŒë¼ë¯¸í„° ìº˜ë¦¬ë¸Œë ˆì´ì…˜, ì—£ì§€ ë°°ì¹˜ì™€ MES/PLM ì—°ë™ì´ ì„±ê³µì  ì ìš©ì˜ í•µì‹¬ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. A physics-based AI digital twin model developed by Swedish researchers precisely tracks battery degradation, including design parameters, and provides SOH/lifetime prediction within 1 second using short charging data. This performance improvement of up to 65%/69% compared to existing methods is useful for fast screening and early anomaly detection in the formation process and EOL inspection, as well as for real-time state management by the BMS and optimization of charging/discharging recipes. From a manufacturing perspective, it strengthens the digital thread connecting design-process-operation data, and has significant strategic adoption value for its ability to lower warranty costs and safety risks. Verification of chemical system diversification, parameter calibration, edge deployment, and MES/PLM integration are key to its successful application.

ì‹ í¥ì‹œì¥ì˜ ì „ë ¥Â·ë„¤íŠ¸ì›Œí¬ ë³€ë™ì„±ê³¼ ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë¶ˆì•ˆì •ì„ ê°ì•ˆí•´ ì—£ì§€ ìš°ì„ (offline-first) ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜ì™€ ê²½ëŸ‰ ëª¨ë¸ì„ ì±„íƒí•˜ê³ , ë ˆíŠ¸ë¡œí• ì„¼ì‹±ê³¼ êµ¬ë…í˜•(OPEX)ìœ¼ë¡œ ì´ˆê¸°íˆ¬ì ë¶€ë‹´ì„ ë‚®ì¶”ë©´ SMEê¹Œì§€ í™•ì‚°ì´ ìš©ì´í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ROIê°€ ë¹ ë¥¸ ì˜ˆì§€ë³´ì „(ê³ ê°€Â·ë³‘ëª© ì„¤ë¹„), ë¹„ì „ ê¸°ë°˜ í’ˆì§ˆê²€ì‚¬, ì—ë„ˆì§€Â·ìš©ìˆ˜ ìµœì í™”ì— ë¨¼ì € ì ìš©í•˜ê³ , ì €ì½”ë“œ/ë…¸ì½”ë“œ HMIÂ·í˜„ì§€ì–´ UIë¡œ ì˜¤í¼ë ˆì´í„° ì›Œí¬í”Œë¡œìš°ì— AI ì¶”ì²œì„ ê²°í•©í•˜ë©´ í˜„ì¥ ì±„íƒì„±ê³¼ ìœ ì§€ê´€ë¦¬ì„±ì´ ë†’ì•„ì§‘ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë³µì›ë ¥ì€ ìˆ˜ìš”Â·ì¬ê³ Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ì˜ ìµœì†Œ ë°ì´í„°ë¡œ ì¡°ê¸°ê²½ë³´(ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ ë³€ë™Â·ë¶€í’ˆ ëŒ€ì²´)ë¥¼ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ê³ , OT/IT ë¶„ë¦¬Â·ìµœì†Œê¶Œí•œê³¼ MLOpsë¡œ ë³´ì•ˆÂ·ì¶”ì ì„±ì„ í™•ë³´í•´ ì§€ì†ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ê³¼ ìš´ì˜ ì•ˆì •ì„±ì„ í•¨ê»˜ ë‹¬ì„±í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. To account for power and network volatility and supply chain instability in emerging markets, adopting an edge-first (offline-first) architecture and lightweight models, and lowering the initial investment burden through retrofit sensing and subscription-based (OPEX) services, facilitates widespread adoption even by SMEs. Prioritizing application to fast-ROI predictive maintenance (for high-value and bottleneck equipment), vision-based quality inspection, and energy and water optimization, and integrating low-code/no-code HMI and local language UIs with AI recommendations into operator workflows, will enhance field adoption and maintainability. Supply chain resilience can be built by establishing early warnings (for lead time fluctuations and parts substitution) using minimal data on demand, inventory, and logistics, and by ensuring security and traceability through OT/IT separation, the principle of least privilege, and MLOps, thereby achieving both sustainability and operational stability.

The $350 billion investment between Korea and the U.S. ($200 billion for semiconductors and AI infrastructure) will accelerate the North America-centric reorganization of production and packaging. From a manufacturing perspective, the key points are: 1) US localization and vendor diversification strategy 2) HBM-centric advanced packaging/test automation and enhanced yield/traceability 3) SKU segregation and origin/parameter tracking in response to tariff and export control volatility 4) Supply risk mitigation through co-validation of equipment and materials and multi-regional inventory 5) TCO optimization linked to energy and decarbonization, including green hydrogen 6) Advanced demand and capacity planning based on APS/digital twin, reflecting hyperscaler CAPEX signals. It is considered a useful reference for strategy and trend identification and mid-to-long-term investment decision-making.

Dyson Farm's AI x Energy 'Dual Transformation' presents an execution model that, even in manufacturing, integrates multi-factory, warehouse, and mobile equipment into a single platform (EAM/CMMS+IoT+Telematics) for real-time operation and optimization, and advances production automation and quality monitoring with AI, robots, and drones. Simultaneously improve cost, carbon, and resilience with a microgrid that combines biomethanation of process byproducts, wastewater, and waste heat with solar power and energy storage systems, and concurrently implement 'energy-aware scheduling' linked to renewable power generation periods and electrification/biofuel conversion. It is crucial to drive pilot-to-scale-up based on OEE, kWh/Unit, and CO2e/Unit KPIs, and to establish a diffusion mechanism through integrated departmental governance and partnerships.

Dyson Farm's digital, mobility, and energy converged operations provide a significant benchmark for manufacturing AX. This circular system, which integrates 100 farms, warehouses, and equipment onto a platform, deploys AI and robots, and secures self-generated power with biomethane, is directly extensible in manufacturing to multi-factory and fleet integration, energy self-sufficient factories, and by-product energy conversion. Proposals in the Korean context (small autonomous equipment, agrovoltaic solar power, distributed energy, governance integration) can be translated into and implemented in manufacturing as EAM/CMMS+IoT data backbone construction, energy-aware production scheduling, introduction of microgrids/storage, and a diffusion strategy centered on industry associations.

An analysis of AI adoption in India reveals that the root causes of the PoC-to-production gap in manufacturing AI transformation (where 75% of companies conduct PoC and 60% have project-based investment) are legacy integration, lack of data standards, insufficient dedicated personnel, and inadequate governance. Prioritize establishing, within 3â€“6 months, the governance, enterprise-wide data standards, and MLOps/change management systems that 98% of mature companies possess, and design the scaling with edge-first architectures for applications like vision inspection and predictive maintenance, and KPI-based, 'cash-return focused' projects such as OEE and scrap rate.

MSME ëŒ€ìƒìœ¼ë¡  ê²½ëŸ‰ ëª¨ë¸Â·ëª¨ë°”ì¼ í¼ìŠ¤íŠ¸Â·ë‹¤êµ­ì–´Â·êµ¬ë…í˜• ê°€ê²©ìœ¼ë¡œ TCOë¥¼ ë‚®ì¶˜ â€˜ì ˆì•½í˜• AIâ€™ê°€ íš¨ê³¼ì ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. 3â€“6ê°œì›” ë‚´ ì „ì‚¬ ë°ì´í„°/ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ ì²´ê³„ ìˆ˜ë¦½, ì—ì§€ ê¸°ì¤€ ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜ ì„¤ê³„, PoCâ†’ìš´ì˜ ì „í™˜ ê²Œì´íŠ¸ ì„¤ì •, í˜„ì¥-IT-ë°ì´í„° CoE êµ¬ì„±ìœ¼ë¡œ ì‹¤í–‰ë ¥ì„ í™•ë³´í•˜ì„¸ìš”. Through an analysis of India's AI ecosystem, we present scaling, governance, infrastructure, and talent strategies essential for manufacturing AX. Statistics showing that 75% of companies remain at the PoC stage and lack enterprise-wide data standards (18%) and dedicated talent (13%) indicate that the prior establishment of legacy integration, data standardization, MLOps, and change management in manufacturing sites is key to scaling. The high growth of edge data centers (CAGR 19.5%) suggests it's time to deploy in-factory inference, such as vision inspection and predictive maintenance, to the edge. Considering the 51% AI core technical talent gap, upskilling focused on data engineering, cloud/compute optimization, and OT-IT integration is required. For MSMEs, "economical AI" that lowers TCO with lightweight models, mobile-first design, multilingual support, and subscription-based pricing is effective. Secure execution capabilities within 3â€“6 months by establishing an enterprise-wide data/governance system, designing an edge-centric architecture, setting up PoC-to-operations transition gates, and forming a Field-IT-Data Center of Excellence.

In medical device manufacturing, the AI adoption rate in product operations (PLM/QMS, quality and specification management) is about 50% lower compared to other industries due to the burden of regulatory compliance. íœ´ìŠ¤í„´ í­ìŠ¤ì½˜ ì‚¬ë¡€ëŠ” AI ì„œë²„ ì œì¡° ë‚´ì¬í™”ë¥¼ ìœ„í•´ ì´ˆê¸°ë¶€í„° ì§€ì—­ ì»¤ë®¤ë‹ˆí‹° ì¹¼ë¦¬ì§€ì™€ ì—°ê³„í•œ ì¸ì¬ íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸ êµ¬ì¶•ì´ í•µì‹¬ì´ë©°, ì§ë¬´ ì¤‘ì‹¬ ëª¨ë“ˆí˜• ì»¤ë¦¬í˜ëŸ¼ê³¼ ë§ˆì´í¬ë¡œìê²©(ì¼€ì´ë¸”ë§, ESD, IPC/WHMA-A-620)ìœ¼ë¡œ ì±„ìš©-ë°°ì¹˜-ìˆ™ë ¨ ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ì„ ë‹¨ì¶•í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ë³´ì—¬ì¤ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë””ì§€í„¸ ì‘ì—…ì§€ì‹œì„œÂ·AR ë³´ì¡°Â·e-QMSë¡œ í’ˆì§ˆ/ì•ˆì „ êµìœ¡ì„ í‘œì¤€í™”í•˜ê³ , ì—ë„ˆì§€ ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§Â·ë¶€í•˜ê· í˜•Â·ì—´ê´€ë¦¬Â·ì „ì› ë¬´ê²°ì„± ë“±ê³¼ ì—°ê³„í•œ êµìœ¡ì— KPI(kWh/ì‹œìŠ¤í…œ, ì—´ ì¬ì‘ì—…ë¥ , ì „ë ¥ í’ˆì§ˆ ë¶ˆëŸ‰ë¥ )ë¥¼ ë¶€ì—¬í•˜ë©´ TCOì™€ CO2eë¥¼ ë™ì‹œ ì ˆê°í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë˜í•œ ì•½ 4.5ì–µ ë‹¬ëŸ¬ íˆ¬ìë¡œ 9.2ì–µ ë‹¬ëŸ¬ íŒŒê¸‰íš¨ê³¼ì™€ 814ê°œ ê°„ì ‘ ì¼ìë¦¬ë¼ëŠ” ìˆ˜ì¹˜ëŠ” CAPEX-ê³ ìš© íƒ„ë ¥ì„± ë²¤ì¹˜ë§ˆí¬ë¡œ ìœ ìš©í•˜ë©°, ìƒíƒœê³„ íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆì™€ì˜ ê³µë™ ë¦¬í¬ë£¨íŒ…ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¸Œëœë“œ ì¸ì§€ë„ í•œê³„ë¥¼ ë³´ì™„í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. The Houston Foxconn case demonstrates that building a talent pipeline in conjunction with local community colleges from the outset is crucial for AI server manufacturing internalization, and the lead time for recruitment-placement-proficiency can be shortened with job-centric modular curricula and micro-credentials (cabling, ESD, IPC/WHMA-A-620). By standardizing quality/safety education with digital work instructions, AR assistance, and e-QMS, and by assigning KPIs (kWh/system, thermal rework rate, power quality defect rate) to training linked with energy monitoring, load balancing, thermal management, power integrity, etc., TCO and CO2e can be simultaneously reduced. Furthermore, the figures of an approximately $450 million investment leading to $920 million in ripple effects and 814 indirect jobs are useful as a CAPEX-employment elasticity benchmark, and limitations in brand awareness can be compensated for through joint recruiting with ecosystem partners.

í­ìŠ¤ì½˜ì€ íœ´ìŠ¤í„´ì— 4.5ì–µ ë‹¬ëŸ¬ë¥¼ íˆ¬ìí•´ ì• í”ŒÂ·ì—”ë¹„ë””ì•„ìš© AI ì„œë²„ ì œì¡° ì¸ë ¥ì„ ìœ¡ì„±í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì„œë²„ ì¼€ì´ë¸”ë§ê³¼ ì—ë„ˆì§€ íš¨ìœ¨ ì¤‘ì‹¬ì˜ ì§ë¬´êµìœ¡, ì§€ì—­ ëŒ€í•™ê³¼ì˜ í˜‘ë ¥, ìˆ˜ë°± ê°œ ì§ì ‘ ì¼ìë¦¬ì™€ ê°„ì ‘ ê³ ìš© ì°½ì¶œì´ í•µì‹¬ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì—…ì²´ ì…ì¥ì—ì„œëŠ” ëª¨ë“ˆí˜• ì§ë¬´êµìœ¡Â·ë§ˆì´í¬ë¡œìê²© ë„ì…, ë””ì§€í„¸ ì‘ì—…ì§€ì‹œì„œ/AR ê¸°ë°˜ í‘œì¤€í™”, ì—ë„ˆì§€ KPI ë‚´ì¬í™”, ì§€ì—­ íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆì‹­ê³¼ ê³ ìš©ë¸Œëœë”© ê°•í™”ë¡œ NPI ì†ë„Â·í’ˆì§ˆÂ·TCOë¥¼ ë™ì‹œì— ê°œì„ í•  ì‹¤ë¬´ì  ì¸ì‚¬ì´íŠ¸ë¥¼ ì œê³µí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. Foxconn is investing $450 million in Houston to train a workforce for manufacturing AI servers for Apple and NVIDIA. Key elements include job training focused on server cabling and energy efficiency, collaboration with local universities, and the creation of hundreds of direct and indirect jobs. For manufacturers, this provides practical insights to simultaneously improve NPI speed, quality, and TCO through the introduction of modular job training and micro-credentials, standardization based on digital work instructions/AR, internalization of energy KPIs, and strengthening local partnerships and employment branding.

The high growth of AI platforms and Anduril's manufacturing investment signals indicate that AI in manufacturing sites is entering an accelerated phase of transitioning from pilot to large-scale operation. Now, standardize OT/IT integrated lakehouses (Databricks) and real-time streaming pipelines, and design energy-computing co-optimization, such as modular data centers near factories, waste heat recovery, and low-carbon power PPAs, all premised on power and cooling constraints. Simultaneously, automate back-office operations like RFQ, quality documents, and purchase orders using agent-based workflows such as n8n, starting from a limited scope to verify ROI, and control vendor lock-in and cost risks with multimodel and governance.

While this is an investment perspective report, it contains numerous valuable signals for Manufacturing AI Transformation. Large-scale AI infrastructure expansion (power and cooling bottlenecks), the necessity for Lakehouse-based data integration, the potential for autonomous agents in automating knowledge work, and defense manufacturing reshoring (e.g., Anduril's major plant) offer direct implications for short- to medium-term strategy formulation. Practically, we recommend: 1) Evaluating AI power and cooling budgets and on-premise/colocation options, 2) Establishing a Lakehouse roadmap that includes MES/SCADA streaming, 3) Piloting procurement and quality documentation agents, 4) Proactively building out a multimodel and governance framework, and 5) Implementing a stablecoin-based micro- and cross-border payment sandbox under regulatory compliance.

ROK-US shipbuilding cooperation serves as a practical template for the Manufacturing AX roadmap, enhancing supply chain resilience based on dual sourcing and nearshoring by combining the expansion of production capacity within the US with Korea's process and quality capabilities. The implementation priorities include defining common platforms/standards, pre-digitalization of the smart shipyard core (schedule, quality, materials), automation of welding, block assembly, and painting, and establishing a digital thread; concurrently, joint ROK-US development of digital personnel, such as skilled workers combined with data and robotics expertise, must be pursued. As an area for short-term ROI, demonstrating results in US Navy/merchant vessel MRO through predictive maintenance, digital twin, and remote support, and then expanding this to performance-based procurement and PPP, will enable a response to China's competition in scale and delivery time.

The MASGA initiative is a strategy to rebuild shipbuilding capabilities within the United States through ROK-US cooperation, presenting an opportunity to combine the technological and human resource strengths of the Korean shipbuilding industry. From a Manufacturing AX perspective, the key implications are (1) supply chain diversification and nearshoring strategy, (2) smart shipyard construction (standardization, automation, digital thread), (3) advancement of MRO based on predictive maintenance and digital twin, (4) simultaneous development of skilled and digital workforce, and (5) diffusion through PPP and performance-based procurement. However, since specific metrics and implementation cases are lacking, ROI verification through a phased roadmap and pilot projects is required at the implementation stage.

Wistron's AllianceTexas AI infrastructure investment accelerates the combination of AI computing with logistics and manufacturing hubs, and manufacturers must reflect power capacity, cooling (liquid cooling), network, skilled workforce/logistics access, tax incentives, and industrial ecosystems as core criteria in their site and CAPEX decisions. Keeping 2026 operation in mind, plan for the external offloading of high-computation workloads such as scheduling optimization, digital twin, and visual inspection, while simultaneously implementing an edge-cloud hybrid approach that considers latency and data sovereignty, along with energy/carbon management linkage. Furthermore, an AI server, rack, and thermal management partnership with Wistron, an EMS/ODM, and the utilization of local procurement and services can reduce deployment risks and TTM.

Wistron is establishing an AI supercomputing facility (110,000 sq m) in AllianceTexas, Fort Worth, demonstrating that incentives, workforce, and logistics ecosystems are key factors in large-scale AI investment decisions. Simultaneously, a strategy is needed to reduce supply chain risks and technological dependence through workforce retraining focused on robotics software, safety, and system integration competencies.

NVIDIA Spectrum-XGS Ethernet combines geographically distributed data centers into a single AI factory, enabling multi-plant model co-learning, large-scale digital twins, and global quality/equipment analysis to run with predictable performance. It enhances the efficiency of large-scale distributed learning (NCCL) through long-distance congestion control, precise latency/jitter management, and E2E telemetry. When applied, it is practical to maintain edge inference while implementing this solution as a backbone, along with PoC and ROI comparisons (versus InfiniBand/standard Ethernet), WAN SLO, and data sovereignty design.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
NVIDIA Spectrum-XGS Ethernetì€ ì§€ë¦¬ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¶„ì‚°ëœ ë°ì´í„°ì„¼í„°ë¥¼ í•˜ë‚˜ì˜ ëŒ€ê·œëª¨ AI í´ëŸ¬ìŠ¤í„°ì²˜ëŸ¼ ë¬¶ì–´ì£¼ëŠ” ì´ë”ë„· í™•ì¥ ê¸°ìˆ ë¡œ, ì¥ê±°ë¦¬ í˜¼ì¡ ì œì–´Â·ì •ë°€ ì§€ì—° ê´€ë¦¬Â·ì—”ë“œíˆ¬ì—”ë“œ í…”ë ˆë©”íŠ¸ë¦¬ë¡œ ëŒ€ê·œëª¨ ë¶„ì‚° í•™ìŠµì˜ ì˜ˆì¸¡ ê°€ëŠ¥í•œ ì„±ëŠ¥ì„ ëª©í‘œë¡œ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì‚¬ëŠ” ê¸€ë¡œë²Œ í”ŒëœíŠ¸ ê°„ ëª¨ë¸ í•™ìŠµ/ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ ì‹œë®¬ë ˆì´ì…˜/ëª¨ë¸ ë°°í¬ ë°±ë³¸ìœ¼ë¡œ ê²€í† í•  ê°€ì¹˜ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë‹¤ë§Œ ì£¼ë¡œ í•™ìŠµÂ·ì§‘ì•½ í†µì‹  ì›Œí¬ë¡œë“œì— ìœ íš¨í•˜ê³ , í˜„ì¥ ì¸í¼ëŸ°ìŠ¤ëŠ” ì—£ì§€ì— ë‘ëŠ” í•˜ì´ë¸Œë¦¬ë“œ êµ¬ì¡°ê°€ ì í•©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë„ì… ì‹œ GPU ê·œëª¨ì™€ NCCL í†µì‹  íŒ¨í„´, WAN ì§€ì—°Â·ì§€í„° SLO, ëª¨ë‹ˆí„°ë§ ì²´ê³„, TCO(í‘œì¤€ ì´ë”ë„·Â·InfiniBandÂ·í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ëŒ€ì•ˆê³¼ ë¹„êµ), ë°ì´í„° ì£¼ê¶Œ ì´ìŠˆë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•œ ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜Â·ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ ì„¤ê³„ë¥¼ ë³‘í–‰í•˜ì„¸ìš”. í™ë³´ ì„±ê²©ì´ ê°•í•´ êµ¬ì²´ ì§€í‘œëŠ” ì œí•œì ì´ë¯€ë¡œ PoCë¡œ ì„±ëŠ¥Â·ì•ˆì •ì„±Â·ìš´ì˜ ìë™í™” íš¨ê³¼ë¥¼ ê²€ì¦í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ë°”ëŒì§í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. NVIDIA Spectrum-XGS Ethernet is an Ethernet extension technology that connects geographically dispersed data centers as if they were a single large-scale AI cluster. It aims for predictable performance in large-scale distributed learning through long-distance congestion control, precise latency management, and end-to-end telemetry. Manufacturers should consider it as a backbone for model training, digital twin simulation, and model deployment between global plants. However, it is primarily effective for training and communication-intensive workloads, and a hybrid architecture, where on-site inference is placed at the edge, is suitable. Upon adoption, concurrently design the architecture and governance, including GPU scale, NCCL communication patterns, WAN latency and jitter SLOs, monitoring framework, TCO (compared to standard Ethernet, InfiniBand, and cloud alternatives), and data sovereignty issues. Due to its strong promotional nature, specific metrics are limited, so it is desirable to verify performance, stability, and operational automation effects through a PoC.

This syllabus organizes construction BIM/digital twin methodologies into an executable roadmap transferable to manufacturing AX, allowing for the construction of brownfield as-is models through reality capture, the pre-elimination of layout, MEP, and piping interferences through multi-disciplinary model coordination and clash review, and the verification of equipment installation, relocation, and shutdown risks with 4D (schedule) simulation. Furthermore, by implementing equipment library and layout automation through parametric/generative design and scripting, and by integrating education, remote collaboration, and operation verification with CDE/cloud collaboration and VR/AR-digital twin integration, decision-making speed and rework rates can be improved.

Abandon the obsession with full automation and switch to Human-In-The-Loop (HITL) collaborative AIâ€”focusing on on-site copilots (equipment setup, process parameter suggestions, exception handling guidance), standardize the responsibility and approval system of AI suggestion â†’ operator approval â†’ execution. The KPI should not be the automation rate, but rather decision support accuracy, reduction of response lead time, and decrease in defects and downtime, and rather than high-precision labeling, strengthen real-time contextualization using operational documents, operation history, and alarm logs. For cobots, visual inspection, and predictive maintenance, implement phased automation by embedding boundary conditions and fail-safes, and prepare for the next 10 years by redesigning roles from operator to on-site dispatcher/validator through training and change management.

This article presents a strategic perspective that AI should be designed as a 'tool that collaborates with humans' rather than a means of complete automation. In manufacturing, HITL-centric applications such as worker copilots, exception handling support, and quality/maintenance decision-making assistance are practical, and establishing boundaries for safety and quality responsibilities, KPI based on augmented metrics, and phased automation expansion are key implementation points. On the premise of a digital thread linking pharmaceutical R&D, manufacturing, and the cold chain, this paper proposes an implementation roadmap that combines QbD/DOE and ML to cover the linking of Critical Process Parameters (CPPs) to Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs), PAT-based real-time predictive control and anomaly detection, and application to continuous manufacturing. Examples such as mRNA LNP, controlled release, and inhalants are directly extensible to multi-objective optimization of nano/precision processes and smart factory-type customized production; upon adoption, GMP-level reliability management, including XAI, federated learning, and model validation, is essential. In the supply chain, building a data pipeline that reduces disposal and recall risks through demand and cold chain temperature deviation prediction and alerts is effective.

This paper comprehensively reviews innovations in drug delivery utilizing AI/ML and presents applicable implications for pharmaceutical manufacturing AX. By connecting process variables and quality attributes of complex formulations such as nanoparticles and inhalers with ML, it accelerates QbD/DOE-based optimization and demonstrates the potential for real-time quality assurance combined with PAT and predictive control in continuous manufacturing. Cases such as Moderna's LNP optimization, MIT's release prediction, and Bayer's inhaler example are useful as reference materials for multipurpose optimization and simulation-based process design. Furthermore, by emphasizing improvements in the supply chain, such as cold chain demand and temperature excursion prediction, and strategies for ensuring regulatory acceptability, including explainability, privacy (federated learning), and model validation, it holds high value for establishing a roadmap for practical implementation.

Although this research is centered on office and HR, it presents a framework directly transplantable to manufacturing AX: by enhancing field acceptance through change management based on TAM/TPB, optimizing demand, material, and human resource allocation through predictive analytics, early quality warning, line/schedule simulation, HR, procurement, and quality document and shift/training RPA, and improving worker performance with skill matrices + adaptive learning. After the pilot, by sharing public KPIs (decision-making lead time, RFT, OEE) and combining governance such as minimum data collection, bias checking, explainability, and RACI, the risks of smart factory transformation can be reduced and its effects can be visualized.

We have defined the mechanism by which AI adoption in the office and HR domains increases decision-making efficiency and employee performance, and systematized an acceptance framework based on TAM/TPB, along with ethics and privacy issues. The manufacturing industry can utilize this to accelerate demand, material, and workforce decision-making, automate HR/quality documents and schedules, and design customized training and feedback for workers. Success conditions include transparent communication, on-site participatory design, and governance that encompasses explainability and bias checking. It is recommended to manage KPIs using metrics such as decision-making lead time, prediction accuracy, contribution to RFT/OEE, training effectiveness, and participation/turnover rates.

By standardizing AI skin diagnosis and self-diagnosis devices at customer touchpoints as edge sensors and linking them with data lakes and demand forecasting (S&OP/APS, CPFR), you can dynamically optimize SKU mix and production plans, and reduce forecasting lead time and errors. Connect the analysis results with the prescription/formulation library to expand to configurable BOM-based low-volume, high-mix and personalized manufacturing, and implement a closed loop of product development â€“ production â€“ feedback through change management automation via PLM-MES integration. Internalize standardized capturing and calibration, MLOps (drift monitoring/re-training), and a personal data consent and anonymization system, and the key is to quantify ROI using metrics such as sales/conversion rate, forecasting accuracy, SKU rationalization, and scrap rate.

The introduction of AI skin diagnosis and consultation in K-beauty retail suggests that by feeding store data back to manufacturing, it can lead to agile manufacturing, including demand sensing, SKU optimization, and rapid formula changes. If generative AI analysis and edge devices are linked together in a standard data pipeline and integrated with S&OP/APS and PLM-MES, it can accelerate personalized manufacturing and closed-loop product development. However, calibration, MLOps, and a personal data protection system must be designed as essential requirements to ensure practical achievements and scalability.
